## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT numerical expression is:
`-0.459914680311301*v*(1 - v**2) - 1.87329057400732*v - 2.49934616662645*x*(0.0579034145056311*t + 1) - 2.49934616662645*x`

Let me expand this:
- `-0.459914680311301*v + 0.459914680311301*v**3 - 1.87329057400732*v - 2.49934616662645*x*0.0579034145056311*t - 2.49934616662645*x - 2.49934616662645*x`

Simplifying:
- v terms: `(-0.459914680311301 - 1.87329057400732)*v = -2.33320525431862*v`
- v³ term: `0.459914680311301*v**3`
- x terms: `-2.49934616662645*x - 2.49934616662645*x = -4.9986923332529*x`
- x*t term: `-2.49934616662645*0.0579034145056311*x*t = -0.144729686*x*t`

So GT = **-2.333*v + 0.4599*v³ - 4.999*x - 0.1447*x*t**

The basis functions in GT are: **v, v³, x, x·t**

Now I need to check each candidate for the ability to represent exactly these four terms (and zero out any extra terms).

Key requirement: The candidate MUST have terms that can produce **x·t** (a product of x and t). Any candidate without an x·t term (or equivalent) cannot match.

Looking through all 50 candidates... Only **Candidate 27** has `cos(c9*t)` which involves t but is not x·t. None of the other candidates contain `t` at all.

Since none of the candidates contain a term proportional to x·t (or any function of t that could produce x·t), **none of them can match the GT**.

Every candidate lacks the x·t cross-term that appears in the GT with a non-zero coefficient. Therefore, no candidate can be equivalent to the GT.
